<Author>etherqueen
<Content>A change for the Worse I stayed at the MO Miami a couple of years ago. At that time, I would say it was fantastic. Sadly, this trip did disappoint. The views of course are still spectacular, and the rooms are nice. The quality of the toiletries in the rooms fell dramatically, to the level one would expect at a Marriott rather than a $450 per day room.. The tv was the old, large kind. There was a small sign in front of it stating that the hotel was in the process of upgrading to Flat screens. One stop at Best Buy could do that in a flash. At first glance the room appeared clean, but when I had to use the room phone, I noticed how really filthy the device was, Yuck.The food was mediocre. I ordered room service with seafood fried rice. There were a few large pieces of shrimp and lobster placed dramatically on top of a squared shaped mound of fried rice. The rice was ordinary at best, the only nod to extravagance was the replacement of peas with edamame.Will I stay again? No thanks. Poor value in spite of the great views.

<Author>AbdullahKuwait
<Content>My absolute favorite hotel in Miami My absolute favorite hotel in Miami I frequently visit Miami and had the chance to stay in several hotels. Having spent 30 nights there over the course of the past 3 years, the Mandarin is my favorite. The main drawback as most people familiar with Miami know is that the hotel does not have a real beach. Also, the pool is a little small. Other than those two things, the hotel is excellent. The staff are very good. Very helpful and friendly. While the staff at Caf茅 Sambal are quite good, they can try to be a little more proactive. For example, at breakfast they see me carrying several plates from the buffet back to my table for my kids and they don鈥檛 volunteer to help me, however, when I ask them they do it very eagerly. At breakfast (especially during holidays) it gets crowded and the service can be slow and a little frustrating. The room service menu is VERY limited after 11pm. They are in the process of upgrading the AV equipment and during my most recent stay the equipment in the connecting room for my kids was upgraded but not in the suite. The SPA is AMAZING one of the best in the world. The ambiance is very relaxed. One of the things I look for in a spa is a separate locker/shower from the gym and the pool and at the Mandarin spa the facilities are top notch. They have a large number of treatment room and therapists on hand so getting an appointment is not a challenge. Even though it does not have a real beach its is on a small key/island and is very well integrated with the surroundings. There is a very pleasant walkway circling the island and it鈥檚 a good 30 min walk. There is a small park with kids playground that the island residents use and my kids love going there. The concierge were very helpful in making my arrangements but they really put a big surcharge on transport and car hire. The hotel has an amazing lobby with breathtaking views of the ocean and the Miami skyline. During prior stays it was very lively with good food and beverage service and live entertainment (afternoon/evening), however, during my most recent stay I hardly noticed any live entertainment or food service. I found out coincidently that the hotel has an arrangement with a nice beach club on Miami beach (South Beach) which hotel guests can use, however, I wish they made this more obvious. Overall, its an excellent hotel, with some room for improvement.

<Author>MacyLondon
<Content>An oasis of calm!! I'd give this hotel four and a half points if half points were possible!. I've subtracted half a point merely because the hotel is expensive, and you will need to get a cab whenever you want to go out to the shops or bars (south beach is around 20 minutes drive). BUT if you're happy to relax in the hotel - or if you're a business traveller - it's perfect. You cannot fail to feel pampered and relaxed. We thought the service was impeccable and I was surprised to read some of the negative comments. Every member of staff (front desk, spa staff and pool staff) were focused on making sure we had a comfortable stay. We loved the complimentary smoothie samples by the side of the pool!! I would also recommend Azul (the hotel restaurant) which serves delicious asian fusion food and fantastic wine.

<Author>Cruzan22
<Content>Hype...Just a Lil We just completed a seven night stay at the Mandarin in Miami. Overall we were pleased with the stay but felt the hotel did not live up to our expectation of service from a Mandarin. Noone ever addressed us by name. I thought that was a signature for Mandarin. The service is definitely on the cold side except for the housekeepers They worked very hard and were always asking us if everything was okay and if we needed anything. They were just great.Front Desk left a lot to be desired, especially considering the usual standards of Mandarin Hotels. We asked on numerous occassions that the luggage needed to be brought up, but time and after time they forgot and we had to call and ask again. One morning we were awakened in error by a wake up call that was meant for another room. They apologized for the error.The hotel lobby and pool grounds are beautiful. The rooms are medium size, well appointed, and views are okay, nothing too great. There is construction going on next to the hotel and there are two big construction cranes. We could see one of the cranes from our room.The food and drinks at the pool were pretty good but nothing fabulous.I did not see anyone using the pool with the palm trees in it. They never offered to set our chairs up in that pool as it pictured on the web site photos. The pool with the palm trees is much smaller that you would think from looking at the web site photos.The hotel is a great respite from the constant action on South Beach. Every time I entered the hotel I felt like I was in my own sanctuary. Very quiet, great smells fill the air, it really is a relaxing environment.Free bottles of water at the valet desk and use of hotel umbrellas is also a nice touch.We went to the health club on a few days, it is very large and seems to have all the equipment one could need. The views of the city are nice, expect for the building across the stree that is under construction.We spent a lot on cabs, but felt the cab service we received was very good.We secured a great room rate throught Travelocity, we paid $200/night for all seven nights.We enjoyed our stay but really have to say that we were disappointed that the hotel did not meet our preconceived notion of Mandarin service standards.

<Author>TB123
<Content>Disappointing I recently stayed 4 nights at the Mandarin Oriental in Miami and to be honest I鈥檓 glad it was only 4 nights. True the hotel is a spectacular building in a fabulous location however the moment you enter you can鈥檛 help but feel that something is missing. The entrance lobby is has floor to ceiling glazing which offers fantastic views across the bay but little else. The large open space doubles as the hotel bar which lacks any kind of atmosphere, that been said, the rooms are large and very comfortable with fantastic bathrooms and great views from the balcony. The pool area is small and the pool (almost an infinity pool) is not heated and is consequently pretty cold. Incidentally the comments from other tripadvisor reports is unfortunately inaccurate, the service around the pool area is not just poor its pretty much non-existent. On all but one occasion I had to make up my own sun lounger and get my own drinks from the bar, my only comfort was the fact that this was the case for most pool users, unless they happened to look like a movie star or a model.With the exception of a couple of the valet parking guys I would best describe the Mandarin鈥檚 staff as being aloof and unhelpful. There are on two restaurants plus pool caf茅 at the Mandarin which given the fact that it鈥檚 located on an island and a good walk 10 min walk from alternatives, means that choice is strictly limited. Despite this fact the food is very good, expensive but very good. I would strongly advise making a reservation at the Azul restaurant as this does get very busy especially over the weekend. A great alternative to the hotel restaurants is the Island Market Place, a small super market / deli that serve good coffee and hot food as well as some fantastic sandwiches. The Island market place is a short walk form the hotel towards the centre of Brickell Key 鈥?I would urge you to try it.On a number of occasions I found myself being disappointed by the Mandarin. These disappointments largely relating to the fact that I felt I was being exploited. For example;鈥here are no tea and coffee making facilities in the rooms or complimentary drinks in the lobby which means if you fancy a drink you have to pay $7 for a coffee from the restaurant.鈥?Distilled water was placed in the rooms however if you wanted spring water it was in the mini bar and was chargeable 鈥?penny pinching!鈥?Internet access was charged at $15 a day.I would expect the above to be complimentary in any half-descent hotel, but for some reason the Mandarin considers itself to be far too superior to offer these amenities to its guests. The Mandarin Oriental Miami could be a fantastic hotel it has a great location and has good rooms however the attitude of the hotel staff really lets this place down. If I go back to Miami I鈥檒l be staying elsewhere.

<Author>hudson67
<Content>Great choice for liesure or business Just back from 4 nights in Miami staying at the Mandarin. This is a great hotel if you want to have excellent service, large rooms, luxury amenities and don't mind driving 20min to where there is more action. The concierge was able to ensure access to the happening hotel bars in South Beach so no need to stay at a hotel that doubles for a club. The hotel is on a little jetty so many of the rooms either look on to the causeway or else downtown miami and both are lovely views. Great gym, nice pool and there is a lovely small fake beach with big beds to snooze on under the palm trees. Didn't use the spa in the end (and they were a bit odd in not wanting to let me view it unless i was going to use it) but it had a large selection of treatment - albeit very expensive. Meal either for breakfast or by the pool were delicious and I would particularily note the excellent quality sushi. Only 15 from the airport and just about 15 min to anywhere we went. Valet parking was swift and efficent. Only complaint was that housekeeping forgot to make up the room 2x in the 4 but management sent a bottle of wine as an apology so no grudges. Although they couldn't give us a late check out past 1pm, they stored our luggage and provide access to a another room to shower and change before our flight. This was indeed a top quality service experience all around - even put 2 chilled bottles of water in our car for the drive to the airport.

<Author>lovetotravelhk
<Content>Not quite the MO I booked (what I thought) was a good internet rate direct with the hotel online at $200 a night. When I checked out 3 nights later, the bill for food, spa and the fixed 18% gratuity cost me over DOUBLE of what my room cost! The staff did try their best, but I don't think their service warranted the 18% gratuity I was forced to pay at the restaurant , room service and spa.Whilst this hotel was a fairly decent hotel, the image on their website is decidedly different to the actual hotel. If you saw a private beach on the website, you will be surprised to find something similar to a sandpit with a couple of deck chairs and a few sad looking cabanas. The pool was small and chairs were placed closely together. The Spa was a reasonably sized where I had body, face and hand treatments. I had to shuffle between 3 different rooms, which defeats the purpose of relaxing, having to dress, undress and walk around the spa to get from one room to another.I was surprised the hotel room just had a bulky old TV that didn't even have an entertainment system. No movies or music on demand. The selections on TV were similar to those found in Holiday Inns. Complimentary toiletries were very limited - just had shampoo, conditioner, soap and lotion. The bathroom had a big bath, but no bubble bath to put in for a good soak. The tap on the sink didn't extend long enough into the sink, so water went everywhere when you tried to wash your hands. The gym was located in a weird place - by a door next to the M Bar (!?) Or you can go via the Spa by lift. This hotel is nothing to rave about for the price that I ended up having to pay for the extra services. It was not quite the MO experience I was expecting being from Hong Kong.

<Author>MrMouseNewYork
<Content>Service Not Good Enough at Mandarin - Lauran Childs and Prime 112 Trump Again! The Mandarin has the reputation of having the best service in Miami, but it's still a shocker!Quite a nice hotel - we liked our room, and the bay view, although hearing the noisy hotel guests next door was not a pleasure. Obviously the Mandarin needs to sound proof it's rooms, as should most hotels.Service around the pool is terrible. If you can get the attention of a waiting person, they will often nod their heads and say yes, they'll get your order - and then it doesn't appear. Some friends of ours arrived and wanted a drink above the pool, and had all manner of problems getting served there, including being ignored. When eventually they got a drink the champagne was served in a plastic glass, even though they were well away from the pool. Not good.Other than that, it was a delight to be able to go to see Lauran Childs' art studio again in South Beach (www.MiamiArt.biz). One evening we went there and bought a couple more paintings, then went on to Prime 112, which had wonderful food, of course.Service in the Mandarin is slow and often inefficient - for example room orders were often not quite right, although I might specify, for example, that I want warm milk with my coffee, then cold milk would arrive. This is not acceptable for a luxury hotel.

<Author>jy99
<Content>Good for relaxing but far from everything else I went here with my boyfriend in June for a short 3 day trip. We were really excited because we had seen all the pictures on the website and of course Mandarin has a great reputation. They happened to have a cheaper rate that weekend so we decided to book this location.The GOOD things first - The hotel is beautiful - the lobby was clean with modern decorations and very sophisticated. The people in the lobby were helpful (although a little too helpful wanting to take your luggage for the tip). We checked into our room and it was beautiful - the bathroom especially. There was an opening between the room and window that could be closed with a shade. A glass shower, tub and bathroom closet. The not so good things - Pool is NOT what is pictured on their website. I was expecting a huge large pool, but it was really small. There weren't that many chairs, and if you didn't get there in time there was no room. Drinks were way overpriced. The private beach area they claim to have is just a small man made area of sand (no water to even go into) and some beds / chairs. Hotel is very far from everything else. Very few restaurants in walking distance and cabs were really expensive to get into the main part of Miami.Would recommend this hotel for those wanting to just stay at the hotel and only relax there. If you are wanting to experience the rest of Miami, go to the beaches, go out, not the hotel to stay at. We probably spent more money on cabs than food.

<Author>eaglesham
<Content>honeymoon heaven Staying at the Mandarin Oriental in Miami for our honeymoon was truely a wonderful experience. From the moment you walk into the foyer, you enter a calming, relaxed environment. We found the staff to be very friendly and extremely approachable. The concierge provided great information on restaurants to visit. Staff at the pool and the beach were very attentive, making up beds and bringing water throughout the day. The beach is beautiful and extremely relaxing and the pool and outdoor spa bath also ideal.The rooms were extremely spacious,especially the bathroom and were kept immaculately clean by the maids who visited twice daily. Every day, a goodnight mat was left on the floor, alongside a next day weather report and a quote with an orchid. each of these little touches added to the experience.The views were simply stunning looking over biscayne bay.Although the hotel is located in downtown Miami and requires transport to South beach, the superb facilties at the hotel encourage you to spend most of your time at the hotel which we did. There are plenty of places near to the hotel to eat and drink, one of the best being the Rosa mexicana only a 5 minute walk from the hotel.I would definately recommend staying at the Mandarin in Miami as I found it to be very luxurious. I am now looking at staying at one of the hotels in another country as I thoroughly enjoyed my holiday in the Mandarin in Miami.

<Author>Brian&Alan
<Content>Nice Hotel but.... I stayed at the hotel recently for 3 nights. The Hotel location was a disappointment. Although you have a nice view over Biscayne Bay, I would have preferred to be on South Beach which was a $25 cab ride each way. The hotel is not really up to the usual Mandarin Oriental standard. Having stayed at Mandarin Oriental properties in Asia, this one looks dated. The rooms are nothing special. Very little asian influence and very bland. The bathrooms are a good size and well equipped, but again, nothing special. I guess I have high expectations of Mandarin Oriental and have never been disappointed (up until now). On the plus side, the concierge, and Giselle are worth a mention. She was fantastic in assisting with restaurant reservations and an excellent choice of bars/clubs etc. The pool at the Hotel is also a good size, but again, looks dated. The private beach is really not much bigger then a sand-pit and not at all what I expected! Would I stay here again, well....you know what, probably not. I bet there are other properties in Miami for a similar price but of a much higher standard and in a much better location. I guess to sum up, the hotel was average and more worthy of a Sheraton, but not a typical Mandarin Oriental.

We will remember this trip for a long time This place is expensive no doubt, however, for a SPECIAL experience this is a place to consider. I choose this hotel because it was ranked #1 in Miami, and I now know why. Think of this as an investment in your relationship.

<Content>Very nice hotel, but not for everyone Excellent service, beautiful decor, very attractive setting, lovely ocean view. But for the price, it did not offer what I would look for whether I was there on vacation or business.For this trip I was there on business. I was 'upgraded' to a deluxe room with small balcony and view. But the room had two standard sized DOUBLE beds, not even queen size. For $500 a night, my feet hung off the end of the bed. Room had internet hook-up but no wireless and they charged $15/day for it. C'mon! even the Hampton Inn provides free internet!The pool area was very small for the size of the hotel. There was a private beach area but it is also small and it's man-made so it's not like enjoying a long stretch of Florida Beachfront. Except for being on the water, It's not particularly well situated for much else. It's a cab ride to everything. There's a walking path around the site, but there's no place to walk to. There did not seem to be anything of interest on the city side.On the plus side, the room was well appointed (except for the standard double beds) and had a fabulous bathroom. The conference area was spacious and well organized. We only had buffet style meals so I can't really comment on the food, but our buffet meals were very good.There is a spa but I did not see it and since I'm not into the spa experience, for me it doesn't add value. I did not mind staying since it was business and I wasn't paying, but I would not consider coming back here for my personal holiday.

<Author>Hou_architect
<Content>A tranquil oasis The Mandarin Oriental Miami is a tranquil oasis. If you are not into the hustle, bustle, noise and crowds of South Beach, this is a perfect spot. The lobby and restaurants are stunning, and the rooms have a spectacular view of the city and the water. We found the service to be impeccable, and particularly liked the pampering we got poolside- a terry cloth cover for our beach chairs, big fluffy towels, and ice water without having to ask. With our mojitos in hand, we enjoyed the view of the infinity pool and the boats beyond.The bed was absolutely to die for 鈥?so comfortable we were asleep in about 15 seconds. We also enjoyed the big soaking tub and separate shower in the bathroom. As for nightlife, the hotel bars were attracting a very fashionable crowd on the weekend. If you want to venture beyond the hotel, it is an easy 10-minute walk to get to the 9th Street and South Miami Avenue restaurant area. We had a lovely candlelit meal there at Dolores. The Mandarin is serene and elegant. We would definitely stay there again.

<Author>fstraveler
<Content>Mandarin Oriental, Miami We stayed at the Mandarin Oriental for four nights last August. I have been meaning to write a review, so I figured a few months late is not too bad. We have previously stayed at the Ritz Carlton on South Beach, but wanted to try the Mandarin since we heard and read great things. Below is my feedback:** Lobby ** The hotel lobby is really nice. Has a beautiful view of the bay from anywhere you stand. There is also a coffee bar which is available in the mornings and an actual bar available in the evenings for pre/post dinner drinks. ** Location ** This is probably the only complaint I have about the Mandarin. A cab ride to South Beach costs $30 each way and we went out to dinner every night, so it ran between $70 -$80 a night for cabs (this excludes other cab rides while in South Beach). So if you do actually plan to spend most of your time in South Beach, I would highly recommend not staying here. I would recommend the Ritz Carlton on South Beach as the alternative. ** Service ** The service was fairly good. If we had any request (no matter what time of day or night), they would accommodate without issues. The only minor complaint is that they are fairly slow at the restaurants. When we had lunch our first day there, it was so slow that we decided not to eat there again. In terms of the food, it is very Asian based so keep that in mind if you do or do not like Asian food. We thought we loved Asian food, but four days of Asian lunches will take their toll 飦?At the pool, food/drink service was fairly quick, but I think it鈥檚 because the pool was small. We ordered room service each day for breakfast and they do a good job with that. On a side note, definitely check out Barton G restaurant in South Beach. They had a good scene and great food. ** Pool **The pool is actually not that great. It鈥檚 very small and you only get sun all day in half the area. Other areas get covered with shade fairly quickly. Also, as you probably all know, it is not on the beach. They have a little sand area but it feels like a cheap park rather than a man-made beach. Quite random actually. They would have done better by making the pool larger and more luxurious.** Gym ** The gym was excellent. They have new equipment, it鈥檚 very clean, and they provided water, juices, fruit, etc. They also have a path for jogging along the bay which was very nice. ** Spa ** Also excellent. If you are going to the Mandarin to get away and simply get spa treatments and stay at the hotel, I would definitely recommend it. But again, if you are planning on spending time at restaurants in South Beach, it鈥檚 a hassle.** Rooms ** We had a room with a view of the water and the city. For the most part, a majority of the rooms look like they would actually have views. The hotel is fairly new and well kept so that is another positive. It is also very clean. The bath products they provided were great. The only thing to keep in mind is that the bathroom has an open window to the sitting area/bedroom. So if you are not with your spouse/significant other, it may be uncomfortable. You can close it with a little pull-shade, but it鈥檚 still somewhat intrusive. It didn鈥檛 bother us since we are married, but if I was with a friend, it would have been a little uncomfortable.** American Express **For those of you who use the Amex Platinum travel service, the amenity you get is $100 credit towards lunch. You have to use it in the actual restaurant though (of course we didn鈥檛 so we didn鈥檛 get the credit so keep that in mind). You also get the usual free breakfast and late check-out. In terms of the upgrade, we were supposedly upgraded two room types, but I didn鈥檛 see that. Seemed like the same room we booked. So with all that said, if I was staying downtown for work and spending my time there, I would stay here again. If you plan to come to South Beach to go out and go to the beach you are better off at the Ritz Carlton or another hotel directly in South Beach.

The beach area too - Guests would leave books and such on the beds early in the morning and then not show up to use the beds till the afternoon. Ultimately I still enjoyed the hotel, but for the price you are paying they should be able to meet everyone's needs.

<Author>DNewYork
<Content>Best Service in MIami I just spent a week at the Mandarin with my partner and my family and we had a terrific time. The rooms are quite luxurious, the service is divine, and the food always brought a smile to our faces.Room--Very comfortable and spacious with a terrific balcony. I especially liked the marble bathrooms! The beds were very easy on the back and the sheets and linens have thread count galore.Maid Service--One of the best parts of the hotel. Rooms are cleaned in a timely fashion and requests can be made with ease for both daily housekeeping and turn-down service. Who can resist the little orchid bud they leave on your bed each night?Restaurants--Quite tasty. Good Asian fusion and we like how grams of protein and calories are listed for several of the choices. Azul is quite upscale, but the cafe downstairs is simple and consistent.Public Spaces--I loved going down for coffee each morning at the coffee bar across from the front desk. The lobby is filled with light and the faint scent of something delicious always hung in the air. The tranquil music was also a good touch.Service--Yes, yes and yes! Miami is not known for its excellent service, but the Mandarin delivers here. Everyone is gracious and willing to work with you to get it done.Price--A bit tricky here. The hotel isn't cheap and the constant add-ons--from the morning coffee to the expensive lunches--added up fast, but it was worth it....Interesting Side-Trip--Check out the Casa Casuarina, which was the Versace Mansion on South Beach. Now it is a private club and hotel. For $175 a person you can spend the day there through an agreement they have with the Mandarin. Yes, a bit pricey, but when else will you be able to swim in Versace's pool replete with gold tiles? Tacky, sure! But what fun!Overall--A great hotel. Two weeks prior to this trip I stayed at the Four Seasons in Miami. The verdict: stay at the Mandarin.

<Content>One night of pure relaxation Spent one day, evening and morning at the MO Miami in December 07 prior to a flight back to London. <Author>nycflyer
<Content>Excellent Hotel and Staff I stayed at the Mandarin Oriental for a conference, and it was unfortunate I was traveling by myself because the hotel and its location are fantastic.The hotel itself is situated on Biscayne Bay. I was fortunate to get a room facing the bay and took full advantage of the private balcony that comes standard with every room. (Have a room service breakfast on that balcony and you'll know what I mean)The room itself was done in rich mahogany and the bed was extremely comfortable and very sleepworthy. The bathrooms were superlative and done in marble. It was really a nice treat to sleep at night with the windows to the balcony open and the ocean breeze blowing in.In regard to items outside the room, the lounge on the lobby floor of the hotel was superb and as you would expect also provides great views of the bay. The pool scene is also top notch, but the wait service by the pool could have been more timely. There is a walking/jogging path that winds around the hotel and hugs the bay through some adjacent condo buildings.The only minor downside I would state is the ability to walk to anywhere notable from the hotel. Its location on the bay also puts it at almost a required taxi (especially given Miami's heat) to anywhere notable. But taxis are always available and immediately summoned by one of the valets. However, given that significant upside of the views based on the hotel's location, this would be a trade-off I would make anytime.In terms of security, this has to be one of the most secure hotels in which I have ever stayed. First the only reason you would be on the road to the hotel is to visit the hotel---so there is no drive-by traffic at all. In addition, there are security/concierge staff all over the lobby and curbside areas and they know what they are doing. For example, I went out for a run and exited through the back of the hotel but entered back in the front. I looked less than attractive upon my return, but the hotel staff opened all of the doors upon my arrival no questions asked. On the other hand, one of my clients who was dressed in a business suit who was not a guest at the hotel was questioned (in a subtle gracious way) if they could be of assistance, which is hotel code for What the heck are you doing here?Finally and certainly not least is the staff. Absolutely first rate and ranks with the best I have ever experienced. Everyone at the ready to assist, with attentiveness that was both subtle and gracious. As an example, I walked up to the concierge and asked him to FedEx a golf club. (Do you know how hard it is to package a golf club?) Rather than the anticipated drill of filling out numerous forms and time taken for them to find materials, the concierge simply took the club, had me fill out the destination for the club and that was it!! (Of course, the charges were billed to my room) But the whole experience was effortless.Bravo to the Mandarin Oriental...

<Author>escholte
<Content>Great Stay in Downtown Miami We chose the Mandarin Oriental as we felt to old for South Beach and we were glad we made the right choice. The hotel is lovely - all rooms have balconies and we chose the Executive Suite - lots of space and a lovely bathroom. A cab to SoBe was $30 and if you're staying at the M.O. then this is a small price to pay. The service was very good, prices for meals and drinks expensive as you would expect - no point in whinging about a $12 martini if your paying hundreds for the room. For those of us visitors without cars, taxis were easy to get and there is a new complex called Mary Brickell Village which has some good restaurants and is a 10 minute walk away. The in-room facilities have it all, although no flat screen TVs yet. The amenities are Aromatherapy Associates of London - smell of lavender and rose - delightful, conditioner is great. Load of fresh fluffy towels.Pool is a bit small but adequate, the gym well equipped but not used much.Azul was a fantastic meal - delicious contempory food and slick service but the only detractor was that it arrived on a cold plate. The only other detractor was the bar - off to one side of reception and seemed like a last minute thought - slick service and a list of over 200 martini - we were sorry we didn't stay long enough to try them all.

<Author>radtravels
<Content>Five Star All the Way! We just returned from two nights/three days at the Mandarin. It was fabulous. It's worth staying here for the gorgeous views of Biscayne Bay all around. The hotel is located on an island and there is a lovely jogging, park area that can be enjoyed. The locals call this are little manhattan and it is aptly nicknamed. The hotel is very oriental in decor and rather minimalist in design but made for a beautiful building. The room was well appointed, bedding comfortable and a nice balcony. The service was superb on every occasion. We enjoyed the pool area and ate in the restaurants onsite. The only qualifier here is the prices are also 5-star. Valet parking pricey and the cost of drinks at the bar were the highest I've encountered (outside of NY). Also, this is not a resort and not the hotel for you if you are looking for a beach trip to FL. The beach is a short drive away (10 minutes, plus time for find parking). But, if you want a hotel convenient in the city of Miami, with great service this is it.

<Content>Liked the service but ... Have travelled to Miami several times in the past and just stayed at this hotel for the first time on a business trip.I thought that the service was above-average for a Miami hotel. From the reservation process to the arrival, the check-in and check-out, felt as if I had been treated well.Another positive (and negative) is the location. The hotel has views of Biscayne Bay which make for a very peaceful sleeping environment. This perhaps augmented by the balcony which would allow those to open windows and sleep with nice bay air (definitely a plus on cooler evenings). However (as a business person dressed in a suit and tie), I felt a little isolated at the Mandarin given that a taxi is a must if you choose to go anywhere on a normal sunny, humid day.Some not-so-positives:- Toiletries were sub-par compared with other hotels; especially missed were mouthwash and a razor - would it cost that much more to provide these staples? - Bed mattress was sunken; woke up with a back-ache.- Hallways were a bit dark.- Neither lobby bar opened until 5pm. The only other place to get a beer before 5pm is the restaurant on level 2 -- which unfortunately is just not comfortable. Still shaking my head on this one.Overall, I may opt for another hotel next time.

<Author>Jwolu
<Content>Really a grand chain It is difficult to know what to say about this hotel having stayed there with my partner for 5 nights in April on a short break before moving on to NY for a business trip. The rooms are spacious and the bathrooms are a treat. That is the best feature of this hotel. The hotel is situated in barren condo land in the financial district. The guests are definitely of the large chain variety -families etc. As a luxury hotel, it just doesn't quite click.The service is patchy. For example, we had to call for our bags to be delivered to the room. We would have done it ourselves but they had been whipped away when we checked in and then they were forgotten. In the Martini Bar, after ordering and receiving our drinks, we asked for water but it did not arrive, even after Certainly. On the other hand, the young woman on duty mornings at the Concierge's office is excellent.The biggest disappointment is the food. The breakfast is very poor value for money (72 USD for two) with different and therefore additional prices for hot and cold buffets which means you pay a separate and additional price, if you have eggs. The breakfast is very average for this class of hotel with quite poor quality bread and eggs. Hot chocolate and a single portion of toast late in the evening cost 20USD. You are better off leaving the hotel, crossing the road and grabbing breakfast in the local gourmet supermarket. The spa is phenomenally overpriced e.g. 271USD for a massage and you have to arrive 45 minutes before an appointment.

<Author>lagniappe34
<Content>Elegantly Fabulous Our stay at this hotel was an absolute dream. Really. Our room was average-size, but well appointed. It was on the balcony deck, so we had a lovely balocony in which to soak in the wonderful weather. The staff was great. They catered to every request - from numerous mojitos at the pool/beach to extra chocolates every night, they were great. The food was good. Just had the sushi, which was good. Nothing spectacular, just really good quality.  I loved the bath products, LOVED them. The soap, lotion, shampoo and conditioner was great. The gym was adequate, really sufficient. Many hotel gyms, IMO, are subpar and an afterthought, but this one, while small, met every need. A nice feature in the hotel, there were large bottles of Evian water and bowls of fruit (Asian pears - my fave) for the taking. I would stop by before heading out for the day get some water and a pear for a snack. The spa was exquisite. Guests get complimentary use of the spa and it was really nice. Boyfriend and I both took steams after working out and the entire spa experience was just sublime. I really enjoyed the pool/beach area. The Mandarin has a a great little beach area on the bay and it's fabulous. They have those great, big beds on which to lay and it's just so relaxing. One thing I didn't like (and it drives me crazy at all hotels), they charge $5 per 15 minutes for internet usage. I know it sounds petty, but when I am paying $500 for a hotel room, for a property to charge so exorbitantly for internet time is just petty. But they're making money, so I would do the same if I was in that position. Overall a remarkably relaxing, special stay. Cannot wait to return.

<Author>amizu
<Content>Mandarin Oriental Miami = dreamy I just spent a night at the Mandarin Oriental - Miami this past weekend as an escape from South Beach where I live, and also to celebrate a birthday. From start to finish the experience was dreamy. I had read that service could be iffy, that the pool was small and cramped, and that the bill might include extra charges. The pool was area was small and cramped (but the pool itself was empty), but the service was fantastic and the bill was correct.When we checked in we did not wait at all, and the very friendly man at the front desk (Raul) brought us up to our room, which had been upgraded to a junior suite with a huge balcony and a great bathroom. It's true that the bathroom (tub, sink, shower) are open to the bedroom with a screen that can be lowered, but the toilet is separate and has a door. We liked the unique design feature because it made the room feel even bigger (but then again, we got up at the same time as each other). The TV was old and had no movies (but we weren't there for that, so we did not mind.) Five minutes after we entered our room, just as we were cracking open some champagne, room service brought up a delicious birthday cake as a surprise! (There was also a box of chocolates, which I presume is always there.) Turn down service that night left us bottles of designer water as well. That night we ate at Azul, and the great service continued. (Another birthday surprise after dinner too!) The 2 sommeliers were attentive and helpful. The food was delicious - I particularly recommend the rainbow of oysters appetizer if it's still on the menu, ditto the salmon tartare and the surf and turf. The scotch selection was impressive. The scotch was brought along with a cup of ice each, so we could control how much ice we wanted - nice touch. The cheese selection, on the other hand, was weak. There were only 5 options, and 1 was out. Still, overall a fun, delicious experience.The next morning we ate at Cafe Sambal. The food was good, but exactly the same prices as room service - in other words, overpriced. It was a bit chilly in the morning and the maitre d' noticed I was cold and offered to bring me a wrap - another nice touch. The individual syrup was also warmed up - again, nice touch. The buffet did not look particularly appealing, so we ordered from the menu and were happy with what we received.We spent the day at the beach, enjoying the raised beds and hammocks. The attendants were great - not intrusive, but they did bring us water frequently. At the pool (where we went to each lunch and to swim a bit) the attendants provided ipods, magazines, water, mango sorbet, etc. For lunch we ate sushi which we found generally to be overpriced and not particularly appealing. After the beach we took advantage of the spa by booking a couple's suite for a few hours. As spa waiting areas go, I expected a bit more, but it was relaxing. There are two showers, which separate the sauna from the steam room. No jacuzzi. I would have preferred to have showers near the lockers  vanities. The 2 toilets were also separate from the lockers  the showers. The relaxation area itself was pleasant, although there was a guest snapping pictures, and talking on the phone! Anyway, the couple's suite massage treatments were delightful. We started out with rose petal foot treatments, while we watched dolphins dancing in the bay below. Next we chose to have sea salt exfoliation scrubs, then massages (aromatherapy  hot stone  swedish for me, deep tissue for him), then clay scalp massages. In between the salt exfoliation and the massages, the massage therapists exited the room so that we could shower (in the suite) and return clean to our massage tables. An absolute delight.Overall, despite the hefty price, I heartily recommend the hotel for spa, dinner at Azul, romantic getaway or just rejuvenation in general.

<Author>MartinJH
<Content>One of the top three in Miami Definitely in the top three hotels in the Miami area - I have stayed at most of the decent hotels in the last couple of years. The Setai is the best (and most expensive by a long way) and then it's between the Mandarin and the Four Seasons for second. The Mandarin wins in terms of style and facilities, the Four Seasons on pool area. The Ritz Carlton would be next and then the Shore Club, Delano, Victor, etc. below that.For my long weekend stay, was given a Bay View King room on a lower floor, which gave good 90% view over bay towards Miami Beach, and a decent sized terrace with loungers. Room was asian-infludenced in style and consisted of large room with separate bathroom with a bath and a shower. Room amenities were a bit sparse for a 5-star room (standard shower kit, etc.) with no handy extras (razor, ear-cleaners, etc). Also the TV only had standard cable channels (plus a couple of premium movie channels) but no pay-per-view.Pool and outdoor area are small and slightly cramped - we visited during half-full weekend and by 10am all the beach chairs were full and packed in like sardines. The beach-area, outside gate across path, with a few cabanas and beach-beds, is much better - it gives you a better view, is quieter and you have more space and sand between your feet. Pool menu is asian-based and while not extensive was of a good quality.Breakfast at Cafe Sambal is a good option - an extensive menu at decent prices and there's both inside and terrace tables - note: the outdoor tables get very busy and the queue one morning was 30 mins.The 2 main bars at the Mandarin (Lobby and Bar M) are small and disappointing and should be avoided for all but an emergency last-minute drink.Service was impeccable at all times - e.g. lady delivering breakfast set up the table on the terrace at our request, and upon spilling a few drops of milk on the table, came back 5 minutes later with more milk and a few extra pastries.If you have the money, stay at the Setai. If you want 5-star luxury and to lie by the pool, stay at the Four Seasons. if you want 5-star luxury and impeccable service and style, stay at the Mandarin Oriental.

<Author>NYCtravel
<Content>Well below expectations My husband and I stayed at the Mandarin for 3 nights at the end of February. We were assigned a room, and told that the bellman would be up with our luggage shortly. Unfortunately, when we got up to the room, we realized that we were not the only guests staying there - someone's whole luggage (including a women's purse) was spread out in the room. We went downstairs, received a lukewarm apology (the bellman was more apologetic about the situation), and were assigned another room - turns out this one is a lower category than what we paid for! My husband called the front desk, where they told him that the hotel was completely sold out and that the soonest they would be able to move us would be hopefully the next day - after I got on the phone (I am currently 5 months pregnant and had just about enough for one day) they said that a bellman would be up right away with a new key for another room. It took 2 more calls and a total of 45 minutes to have this happen.More unpleasantries. There was another guest staying in the hotel with the same last name as me. Surely something that happens quite often in large places, as my name is not uncommon. This issue, however, was too much for the Mandarin staff. The front desk, the spa, the concierge and even the pool bar ALL confused our names, despite the fact that every time I called I left my room number. We received the other guests confirmations for spa appointments, were billed for their food, given their restaurant reservations. Again, a barely lukewarm apology from the front desk regarding our issues at checkout, even as they were taking the other guests charges off our bill.Also, the directions the concierge desk gave to any location were always wrong - this was shocking to us since there were multiple staff giving us directions at different times!We did try the spa, and found both therapists very good for the massages (I had the prenatal massage, my husband deep tissue).We would not return to this location, rather opting for the Four Seasons where our experiences have always been positive. Further, based on this stay, I doubt we would ever stay at the Mandarin chain again.

<Content>very enjoyable stayed at the MO Miami for two nights in february. this is the 8th time we've stayed at the hotel and we always enjoy it. Summary: MO Miami has excellent design, a very relaxing and tranquil location, but the service level keeps it from rating 5-stars. Food: Ate at Azul - always excellent. The food as well as the service from the wait staff and somalier were great. They do a great job with both fish and meat selections and have an really fantastic wine list. Also notable - great selections from room service - pad thai and shrimp dumplings were fantastic and a nice alternative to the usual room service fare. Deliveries were always within 30 mins of ordering. Beach: They brought in a lot of sand to create a beach area with very comfortable lounge beds and great food/drinks service. You can't get access to the ocean from here, but the view is relaxing and they do a nice job pampering the guests. Pool: smallish pool with lots of chairs packed in. We opted to hang at the beach instead but the pool area was very popular. Service: The only down side. Although room service is very quick, the front desk staff is not up to the same level. We had to call down several times to report that our neighbor was smoking a pipe in his room (we were on a non-smoking floor) and the smell was coming into our room via the balconies. Each time they said they'd call him; finally after the third attempt they actually did and the smoking stopped. Overall: relaxing and enjoyable oasis within downtown miami.

<Author>RLA
<Content>Pretty Good...But... We went to the Mandarin Key Biscayne over Labor Day, 2006. The purpose of our trip was to decompress for 3 days... basically do nothing but sleep in, eat great food, work out and enjoy the spa -- the Mandarin Oriental was pretty on target for our objective. The gym is OUTSTANDING. The Spa is luxurious (expensive, but worth it in our opinion). The bedding was extremely comfortable. And, the service was very, very good.However, the food was not perfect: The casual restaurant is nice -- not great -- but nice. Azul (the fancier restaurant) is above average... not excellent (we actually bellied up to the bar and had the very knowledgeable bar tender wait on us one night, which was the highlight of our Mandarin dining experience for the weekend). The pool-side bar/restaurant is below average, which is consistant with the pool in general....which is why we give this hotel a rating of above average, instead of excellent. If you are looking for a beautiful, spacious pool with wonderful pool-side service, this is NOT the place for you. The pool is almost laughable, so it was a good thing we weren't banking on that for the perfect vacation. For the size of this hotel, they should have a pool that's triple the size with five times more lounge chairs.As well, if you are looking for onsight consistant dining options, this probably isn't for you either. We ended up hiring a car service to bring us to South Beach for dinner (which ended up being worth the 30-40 minute car ride).Bottom line -- if you want a hotel that has a really terrific spa, very nice service and a great gym, and you are ok with 'average' onsight dining options and a below average pool scene, this is a good option for you. If you want an expansive pool scene and multiple onsight dining options, and aren't willing to leave the locale to dine elsewhere, this probably isn't the place for you.Note: There is virtually no beach at the Mandarin Key Biscayne.

<Author>JC&BEB
<Content>Great Hotel, Great Location My Wife and I spent the second week of our honeymoon at the MO, after the Bahamas, in early November 2006. I chose it as Brickell Key was quieter than, but in easy range of South Beach and close enough to the centre of Downtown. (From the airport, it is 15 mins  $25 in a taxi). And because, having spent hours on Tripadvisor, it came out very well. We had a suite (an upgrade!) overlooking the bay - which was amazing, particularly in the early morning and at sunset).The hotel is superbly positioned, the building is very impressive and the staff were, without exception, excellent. They couldn't have been more helpful/ attentive. It is not cheap, but every bit a 5* hotel.We had breakfast each morning in Sambal - great, again, the staff and the food are superb. Supper there was also very good, particularly if you like Sushi. I don't, but found plenty to order instead.We didn't eat at Azul, but people who did, raved about it. The Sushi bar by the pool was also very good and the staff were constantly bringing round chilled water and sorbets - a nice touch.The pool is, as some other reviewers have said, a little small. However, it was never that busy and if the sun beds are a little close together, there were never so many people that it was a problem. (This is a business hotel; I saw more people wearing suits and looking wistfully at the pool than I did actually in it).The spa seemed very popular, though my wife didn't use it, so no personal comment. The gym is very well equipped; a good range of machines and free weights - and never that busy, even at peak times. There is a map with a couple of running routes in the room, which is helpful - a reasonably traffic/ road crossing free route.There is internet in the rooms - if you have a lap top, or about $6 per fifteen minutes at the business centre. Business hotel - what do you expect? There are internet cafes in downtown (10 minute walk) for one dollar per hour.We loved the hotel. It isn't, as several reviewers have said, cheap, but it is definitely 5* in every respect and you get what you pay for. I would certainly recommend it to anybody.

<Author>skrosvik
<Content>Stay somewhere else - waste of money! This hotel is not up to the guiding lines of the Mandarin Oriental hotel chain. A waste of money. Stay somewhere else.My stay was a huge disappointment to my sister and me. We were staying for 5 days. Already at the check-in they assigned us to wrong room. We had booked a deluxe twin bedded room. And we got a king bedded room, but had to change it into a twin bedded room, which they managed to do - after a long wait!!Further on, there were not much deluxe over the room. On the positive side the room was large and had a nice balcony. But it had only very basic things; like an old fashioned television, a cordless telephone (which did not work) and a radio. There were no dvd/cd-player in the room. No international plugs. Nothing extra at all!!! The beds were fine and good size (but I have experienced better beds). But lightening in the room were terrible, no bedside reading lights, and so on. Also, terrible bathroom solution...I mean the bathroom in itself was beautiful, but only thing that seperated the bathroom from the bedroom was a single, thin and sliding screen. So it was impossible to have an early morning shower without waking up my sister. Cause all the bathroom noise goes out to the bedroom. Not very smart solution!!! I prefer privacy when I am in the bathroom and beside this stupid screen there were no locks on the bathroom doors....The housekeeping in this hotels are the worst ever housekeeping I have experienced in any hotel. And it is such a shame that a hotel like Mandarin Oriental offer so poor service to their guests. The second day there were no towels provided, the third day there were no toiletries provided, the fourth day there were no water provided, and the fifth day there were no newspaper provided. I had to call for everything. This is not up to the reputation of the Mandarin Oriental. The business center was nice, but kinda pathetic that they charge you for using the internet there. I think it was 6 USD per 15 minutes, which is very expensive. Food was so-so. Tried the food at the beachside restaurant and in the Sambal Cafe. The sandwich at the beachside restaurant was very plain and tasteless, but the lunch in the Sambal Cafe was quite good.A nice feature on turndown service is that the hotel provides complimentary water from Voss. The onsite spa and pool was very nice, and the best thing about this hotel, I think.The service here is very slow and extremely inefficient. It took them like 30 minutes to get some towels to my room. The doormen outside are more busy talking private stuff, than opening the doors for the guests, you have to stand in line to talk to someone the front desk (which is unusual for a MO-hotel), the concierge is good (when he is actually on his desk). I also find some of the employees to have attitude-issues, which is not proper for a 5-star property. The concierge for example was kinda unpatient and rude when I wanted to ask about the limo-service. And an evening in the pool I was approached by a member of the security staff, and he told me in a very rude way: You have 10 minutes to leave the pool, I think it is kinda rude to talk like this to guests. Where are the humble hospitality?? I was told at the check-in by the manager on-duty that I the pool was official closed at 9 pm, but I could use the pool at my own convenience after this. So, I did at 11 pm. And then this happened. I tried to explain to this guy that I was told something else by the front desk. But he told me something else, and that I had to get out of the pool. I think this guy was very rude, and it is incredible that this can happen. All this made me very angry. I also notified the front-desk about the phone in my room was out of order. They said they would send someone up to look at it right away. But it never happened. I think I reminded them about 4-5 times during my stay, but NOTHING happened.The location of this hotel is depressing and out of nowhere. There is nothing to do there. You better have a car, or prepare use taxi every time you want to go somewhere. You can still walk downtown or to Bayside shopping, which is 25-30 minutes walk away. This was my first visit to Miami, and next time I go to Miami I would rather stay in South Beach/Miami Beach area (Delano Hotel/Setai/Loews Miami Beach Hotel), cause there you will find the points of interests. There is nothing to do downtown, and there are no good shopping options around (except Bayside). You have to go up North Miami or down South Miami or to Miami Beach:)I think this hotel are on a very wrong course, and that the management should be replaced. This is far by the worst 5-star hotel I have ever stayed in, and it is incredible that this can be a member of the MO-chain. Well, I will never return to this hotel. I'd better stick to Four Seasons Miami - which is a beautiful and a serious hotel. Great service at the FS too!! Miami was an amazing experience and a wonderful city, and I will go back without doubt, but not to the Mandarin Oriental!!!I sent a complaint to the hotel manager, but did not receive any reply at all.

<Author>Taskmaster
<Content>Not quite MO Stayed for the third time at this hotel in early October. First time, back in Feb. 2004 we thought it was wonderful - great contrast to just about anything else in Miami. Next time on business thought it was OK but not as sharp as MO ought to be. This latest visit confirmed it. Compared with MO's in Hong Kong, Bangkok and even Singapore this just doesn't get anywhere near. Obviously American service can't touch that of Asia but the rooms can and should be a lot lot sharper for the money. Front desk service just the same as any American chain. No real personality or any attempt to make you feel welcome or special. We do stay quite a lot in MO properties and normally our welcome is effusive. Here we even had to suggest that our AmEx Centurion booking came along with some benefits. Couldn't really see what they were - even to the point of being chased out of the hotel with an attempt to get a 'late charge' for our complimentary continental breakfast!Our upgraded room was remarkably small and ordinary with the view only so so. Water pressure in the shower wasn't very forceful, so quite a big effeort to clean off the soap and shampoo with the very very softened water.Minibar had plenty of gin but no tonic, forcing an order from room service and a truly incredible bill of $ 16.00 (plus tip) for two small bottles.On the plus side the AZUL restauarnt preented us with the best meal we enjoyed on our arduous 10 day (different hotel every night) trip. Super food, very well presented and delightfully served. None too pricey either for the quality.All in all a good hotel but one that does not reach the heights of a hotel group that I have long thought is about the best in the world.

<Author>Greenie2
<Content>Good experience but... I have stayed at the Mandarin Oriental in Miami on 2 separate occasions. The first time (about 2 years ago) was just amazing. We had a beautiful room and were just in awe of the pool, restaurant, service, etc. The second time we stayed at the Mandarin, last year, it was still very nice, but there were a few notable problems and one in particular that still really bothers me. First, the island was riddled with mosquitos at the time. When we ate breakfast at Cafe Sambal, I was eaten alive. But the worst area was the man made beach. When we went down there, mosquitos swarmed around us to a horrific level (picture 6-8 on your body at once), and we turned around and ran back to the pool and jumped into the water for relief. I guess I would have thought they'd post a sign or something at least to warn patrons they were having this problem!The other issue is that instead of locking my purse up in my room while I went to the pool, I buried it in the bottom of my garment bag. The day before we checked out, coming home from the pool, I noticed my bag had been tampered with, but I didn't think anything of it. We ate at Azul that night and we charged everything to the room, so I didn't end up taking out my purse. However, the next day, upon checkout, I took out my purse and noticed that $40 cash was missing! We complained to the hotel and they apologized, but that was it. Sure, part of it was my own stupidity for not locking my bag, but we just felt so comfortable at the hotel. I'm not saying I expected a free night out of the situation or anything, but maybe a gift cert for a lunch at Cafe Sambal or some other token of apology would have been nice. This year, every time we went down to Miami, we just stayed at the Shore Club. There are so many great hotels in Miami, its hard for me to stomach going back to the MO after what happened. I guess I expected a little better customer service there.

<Content>When Expectation is Not equal Perception! Well, I must admit, this particular brand (Mandarin Oriental, MO) demands high expectations! I guess, one can not simply clone a service culture, a culture that has its roots in the Orient. If I may state, compare to the Oriental, Bangkok, this particular property here in Miami really does not seem to have a soul (i.e. Leadership)...though, I must add, the property itself is charming, even some employees, but again, a brand of that caliber ought to be more than just a beautiful building. The way I perceived the property in Miami, I do dare to say, is far from being a soul mate to its flagship in Bangkok. Such traditional brand must not be compared to SoBe standards. If being compared to South Beach Hotels than simply because Mandarin Oriental as a brand failed to deliver its promise: Home away from Home. By reading past comments/comparisons of MO vs. SoBE, I urge every Floridian to visit a MO property in Asia. I do hope that in the not so distant future other oriental brands such as The Peninsula and/or Shangri-La finally bring a property to Miami, so that my fellow Floridian have a chance to truly experience a service culture beyond traditional ratings.Suggestion:聽 Great seeting, building, etc. but again, if you are used to MO service, AVOID this particular property in Miami !!!

<Author>defore4735
<Content>Mandarin Report My wife and I flew down to the Mandarin based upon many of the reviews from this board. Here's my review:Arrival:We arrived at 11 am on a Friday via cab from the airport (about $35 including tip). When we arrived, the attendants were there to greet us and immediately took advantage to look at our luggage tags to identify our name and call us by name as they asked how our trip was (pretty classy). I don't know if the staff has a listing of the expected guests, but it's a nice touch.As we checked in, we were OK if the room wasn't ready. We could simply wait, hang out at the pool. Reception offered us a choice of rooms, so we decided to take a room we could get in immediately. An attendant was immediately available to take our luggage and take us to our room.Room:We had a city view with balcony on the 11th floor. The bed was very comfortable. The attendant introduced us to all the amenties of the room as well as telling us to use the direct connection to the internet. He retrieved ice for us and insisted we call them if we needed anything.The room overlooked Brickell Key Bridge. It was nice enough view of the city and partial bay. We weren't concerned about the view as much as the relaxation aspect of the hotel. We put on our suits and headed down to the poolPool:The pool area is small. I was surprised by how small the area was. They had nice 70's 80's music playing around the pool. It wasn't obnoxious, but occassionally the blender would override the music. They offer complimentary ipods, lotions, cd players, water, sorbet, so you really won't need to want for anything. We would have liked to ordered some drinks, but our attendant never asked if we needed anything for the 2 hours we were there. She simply continued to walk by us. (I'll get back to this later).The menu at the pool has some unique drinks. The primary food served is sushi and it was great. They also have sandwiches and some salads, but nothing like chips/salsa, nachos, or any mexican flair. It is primarily a sushi bar with nice salad presentations, which I believe is perfect for the setting. The manmade beach is nice, but there are several boats that patrol in and out of the bay area. May get a little annoying, but with an ipod, who cares. An attendant can help get you set up for your own private bed to catch the rays, but in the heat of August, it's nice to have the pool nearby.Recreation:The excersize room is mainly for cardio. They have some free weights and some other life fitness machines. It's true you can watch t.v. while you're doing cardio. They provide some fruit and water for your pleasure during your workout. I would have liked to have a few more weight machines, but my workout was just fine. They also have a great little outside walk that runs around Brickell Island that is nice to run. It's a little over a mile, but a great running/walking track.Attendants in the work out area didn't smother or bother you. Depends on what you're looking for.There is a small playground for children, but other than that, there is nothing for them to do. This hotel DOES NOT cater to families. It is designed to be an oasis for the business or weekend travelers. Room:Room was nice. Comfortable bed with lots of pillows. The attendant was very good. They had pull down service at night. There was a little switch you could push if you wanted or didn't want them to make up the room each day or night. Issues: I was surprised to see that the television did not offer movies as an option. The television was your basic television. Someone mentioned the bathroom shower door being an issue, we found that as well. Water would fall off the door onto the floor causing a slippery service. Neither of these were of particuliar concern to us.Room was pretty much what you see on the website.Restaurants:We didn't do Azul's, but we did eat at Cafe Samba. Service was a bit slow but breakfast was good. We didn't do the buffet. We ordered ala cart. We decided to venture out for dinners. We chose Duo on South Miami, a small restaurant with a nice brazillian environment. They offered a variety of foods from seafood, to steak, to lamp, to pork, to duck. The salmon and steak were delicious. I would highly recommend this. We walked BACK from to the hotel after dinner, about 6 blocks. Tab for 2 including drinks $122. The following night we ate at Mortons, about 4 blocks from the hotel. Mortons, is Mortons. I believe I would prefer Duo's.It's nice to walk the streets of Downtown Miami back to the hotel. There's a nice breeze along the bridge back to the Oriental.Issues:We had some issues at the pool. The servers aren't very open to asking you for orders, similar to what you may have at a restaurant. They pretty much leave you alone until you tell them you need something. Some people may like this, but when you can't get one to stop by and offer anything, it's an issue that I raised with management which they addressed and made sure they met with me before leaving.On Sunday, it seemed like family day at the pool. It may have been a layover hotel for the day for these families, but kids were all over the place, the lobby, the pool, the restaurants. These families basically took over the pool and made things very loud. I have 4 kids of my own, but if they get too loud, and they are bothering other people trying to relax, I say something to them. These families didn't do that, so we eventually left and went back to the room.Would we stay there again? Maybe. I think we would try the 4 Seasons or another more posh South Beach hotel.

<Author>jwsmd3
<Content>Cl;ose To Perfection ! Why is it so rare to leave a hotel feeling as satisfied as I was with MOMi? From arrival to departure the staff seems to want only to be sure you are having a perfect stay. Their apparantly liberal policy regarding upgrades and late check out won me over. Isolated (which is exactly what I wanted) on Brickell Key your dining options are limited to the Hotel but breakfasts and dinner at Cafe Sambal were excellent. The AM buffet with coffee and juice for $20 is well worth it. Dinner (did the tasting menu with paired wines) at Azul for a birthday was excellent: entertaining and delicious (am a fish lover but the veal roullade is out of this world) with flawless service and an engaging, informative sommelier who knew exactly when not to intrude!They do not have a resort fee , a policy I detest, and use of the gym and the lockers/ showers/ sauna and steam are free to guests as it should be. A Deep Tissue Massage was done right though the very comfortable high tech mechanised massage table was amusing.My only gripe would be the steepness of that valet parking fee but didn't bother with a rental car til the night before leaving.Note breakfasts/ lunch and poolside barservice incur a standard 18 % tip but I found service almost flawless and (be aware) many Miami establishments routinely do this as many foreigners are used to service compris.Will return.......a worthwhile indulgence!

<Author>tktm
<Content>Elegant My wife, myself and 2 1/2 year old daughter took a long 4th of July weekend down to Miami, we originally had booked a stay at the Ritz Carlton Key Biscayne. We left the Ritz early because of the poor service, small rooms and because the management was requiring guests to wear permanently attached orange vinyl type medical bracelets to access the pool and beach areas. We had American Express' Fine Resorts and Hotels program cancel the rest of the Ritz stay and move us to the Mandarin Oriental Miami. What a wonderful decision that ended up being!!!!The Mandarin Oriental Miami is just simply OUTSTANDING, they truly understand customer service, their 5 star rating is richly deserved. We were warmly greeted and treated as we entered the hotel. When we checked, in our room was upgraded to a Brickell Suite (via the AMEX Fine resorts program), they told us they had other rooms available if it was not to our liking. As the bellman took us to our room, he was careful to point out the fire exits on our floor, certainly a sign of a well managed hotel. One should note that on the higher floors that the fire escape path may actually lead across the exposed roof of the lower floors.The room was a joy to behold, bamboo flooring, a large living space with couches, chairs, TV, guest bathroom, desk and balcony. This was separated from the sleeping quarters by a very nice piece of cabinetry with sliding rice papered glass doors. The bedroom was equally huge with a wonderful feather bed, nice sound system, TV and balcony. The bedroom had direct access to the master bathroom with a free standing two person tub, dual sinks, and separate shower area. The entire bathroom was well finished with a nice Spanish marble. The bed was VERY nice with a soft feather top. The crib that was sent up to our room was just glorious, a wonderful chrome design lined with goose down, our daughter loved it. (certainly much nicer than the ratty wood thing the Ritz Carlton had)The lovely view from the room was of the bay and the Miami Skyline. My wife enjoyed the spa services. The Spa keeps an oriental motif, the lighting is low, the fragrances are earthy. The steam room and sauna are nice, the whirlpool is outside though, by the swimming pool. The showers in the spa come at you from all angles. The spa has a nice feeling to it, it certainly does not have an industrial feeling.The private island is nice too, there is a running path all the way around the island, a playground area for the kids, and a man made beach. Please note however that there is NO ocean access from the beach. If you want to swim in the ocean, go to the concierge and he/she can set you up with passes to one of the beach clubs in South Beach. The hotel pool is nice, but not huge, it does feature an infinity edge.Dining at hotel was also a treat, first we tried the Sanibel cafe, the food was interesting and the views were relaxing. I suggest trying the mildly hot banana ketchup, and the boneless beef ribs. The service was relaxed, but probably only rated 3.5 stars. The kid's menu was standard fare. The only negative thing I saw at the hotel occurred at the cafe, the sight of an anorexic european woman rubbing her pregnant belly before she lite up her cigarette was unpleasant enough to kill my appetite.We also had dinner the Hotel's 5 star restaurant, AZUL. It defiantly has earned its 5 stars. The food was interesting with a lean towards a seafood bent. The service was just truly gracious. The kids menu is shared with the cafe and again is standard fare and certainly not 5-star.In summary, almost every bit of service in this hotel is spot on perfect. They actually understand what service is, they don't just mimic it. Even as you check out of the hotel, the valet hands you a bag with assort fruits and 2 bottles of water; nothing less than a godsend if your next stop is the Miami International Airport.

<Content>Four stars from this reviewer, 2nd business trip to this hotel I was here on business. This is my second business trip at the hotel. The service at the front desk, spa, gym, restaurants, concierge....all the service people were excellent.I drove over from the west coast of Florida where I reside. The only parking at the hotel is valet which is $30.00 per day which I thought was too high. I didn't care for the food at the hotel which was also too expensive. I liked the gym, the treadmills and stationary bikes each had individual television sets with headphones. There were different newspapers at the gym. There is an attendant in the gym who is very helpful. The sauna and steam room and shower facility is about the best I have experienced, as are the complimentary robes. By the way, there is no additional charge to use the gym, sauna or steam room. The rooms are really beautiful and relatively spacious with spectacular interior decorating, bathrooms, showers, etc.Overall, I would give four stars because of the beautiful rooms, excellent employees, and very luxurious steam room, sauna, and shower facilities.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Probably the best hotel in Miami area We were here for a family wedding on South Beach and rented three separate rooms. This hotel is lovely...very soothing zen-like decor. Nice crisp sheets, rooms are well sound proofed, even the views over the city and bridge are nice. We did not hear any traffic noise from the bridge because we were on a high floor (rooms on the 9th, 14th and 19th floor). Be careful as shower is all glass and does leak water onto very slick marble floor, so use lots of towels. One of us was traveling with a baby, and the room set up was a little awkward for a crib (you couldn't put the baby down in a separate area in their cityview rooms...so there isn't a way to stay up and watch TV once you put the baby down...perhaps a room with a different configuration would've been better). Pool is small but lovely setting overlooking the bay. They have created a small sandy area with beds to lay on by the bay (great views), but they have no real beach. Waitstaff isn't as attentive as they should be...at the pool, they never came by to take drink orders and they should be much more attentive for a resort in this cost category (we had to flag them down when they finally stopped chatting with each other by the bar). A few teensy things you might want to know...don't try to book a room through American Express platinum card travel services...the rate Amex will quote you is at least $200 more per night...go onto the MO hotel's website and click internet rates for the lowest rates. We got a rate of $489 a night and Amex was quoting us $699 a night for the same room. Also, don't buy into the whole Amex upgrades...one in our party was promised a room upgrade upon arival, and this upgraded room was identical to the other rooms we rented at much lower rates (same views, same size). I will say that the front desk staff at this hotel needs improvement. Although they were pleasant at check in, they were clueless...after handing us the keys and telling us we had been given a room far from the elevators, just as we requested, we got off the elevator and our room was next to the elevator bank...some charges ended up on our room that weren't ours but they were promptly removed at check out (like extra valet charges). Valet is $30 a night and you can't self park. Bellhop staff was always eager to help and we never waited more than 2 minutes for our car from the valet. Meals at this hotel are outrageously expensive...if you can avoid eating here, go offsite for your meals. South Beach is only 10-15 minutes away and Ft Lauderdale is no more than a half an hour. It's an easy drive if you fly into Ft Lauderdale airport. I heard horror stories of some South Beach and Ft Lauderdale hotels (we cancelled our reservations at the Westin Diplomat due to Dateline NBC story about bed bugs there), so this is probably one of the most luxurious hotels in the area...but very costly!  
<Date>Apr 11, 2006

<Content>Surely not the best in Miami!! My husband and I stayed recently for one night and were glad it wasn't for more nights. Unluckily, the room was overlooking the bridge/road. *The only bar at the hotel opened at 6pm, could not have a drink or a coffee before then (there was one bar inside the Oriental restaurant, but the smell of raw fish was terrible and it was raining outside). *The choice of restaurants/food was poor (They were there, but they had very non-flexible opening times and you have to hope for good weather). *We decided to order and expresso and a hot chocolate from room service. They are not to be touched, we were told. All these (and a few more) during a one night stay... It might be a Mandarin Oriental, but it lacks of the class, customer service and touch you find in hotels in the Far East. Not worth the money.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Shame about the flight path We stayed at the MO for one week in February whilst the Boat Show, President's Weekend and the Food and Drink Fair were on; consequently the hotel was very busy. There is no doubt that the MO is very luxurious, however be careful that you do not end up with a room overlooking the bridge road, as we did initially before they changed it the day after checking in. The hotel is in 3 sections of a curve and one third of the back section looks over this bridge, so ask for either the centre section or the section overlooking the pool. The reception staff vary in their desire to accommodate any disappointments, so if at first you don't succeed, try again with someone else! It is a particular concern that there is a major flight path right over the hotel, which seems quite bad at certain times of the day: the very expensive breakfast on the terrace was somehow marred by this experience, as were our sessions by the pool. I can't believe no one else has commented on this. Regarding the spa, I paid for a rather useless pilates session: like a previous reviewer, the teacher was a sweet girl and I did not like to complain about her, but I had thought the MO spa would ensure that all their staff were excellent in their field. My final negative comment is that the beach was out of bounds more times than not during our stay due to private parties and the time taken to set up these parties: although it did not bother us, I'm sure some people would mind if this was one of the features which attracted them to the hotel.Despite these comments, our family did enjoy our stay!
