<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Mostly great but a few disappointments We recently spent one night at the Mandarin Oriental Miami. The room was immaculate and attractive. The bathroom is large and open to the room, however you can pull down a shade for privacy. (The toilet was behind a door, at least).The infinity edge pool is really nice and the service all around the hotel was very friendly. My disappointments were: (1) I had an extrememly mediocre massage at thh spa, which normally wouldn't have bothered me so much but because I paid $185, I was expecting a really good one.(2) We ate lunch at Cafe Sambul and the restaurant at the pool and the meals were just average. Again, normally I wouldn't be so nitpicky but because we paid between $70-$90 for the two of us, I was expecting much better food.Overall, a nice hotel but they have you where they want you...that is, if you want the convenience of eating at the hotel, you'll be overcharged. As for the spa, I suppose it is my fault for not complaining, however, I felt uncomfortable complaining because the massage therapist was so nice. I usually rely on the reputation of a place and was never disappointed with a spa service from a top-rated spa until this one.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Amazing honeymoon, Beautiful hotel, great atmosphere. Helpful and polite staff My husband and I stayed in this hotel after reading great reviews about it here. It's all we read and more! Very very helpful and kind staff. Definitely first class. The rooms are cleaned once in the morning and once in the evening and they leave an orchids in your bed) The bathroom is very spacious. The Decoration in the room is modern and it gives you a feeling of 'tranquility'.No, the hotel is not the cheapest, but we don't regret it since we had a great time. You pay for quality :) and since we were honeymooners we got an upgrade of room on arrival which was great.And the atmosphere!! they have different soothing instruments being played at the lobby every day (harp for instance). Very nice.It's not very close to south beach, which for people that loves to party might be inconvenient... NOT FOR US though. You can always grab a taxi (they ARE expensive around 25dlls to drive you there), the hotel will arrange one to pick you up within a couple of minutes.They have a couple of restaurants in the hotel, they are good. But if you are in Miami you might want to explore a variety of food there, many restaurants at better prices. If you don't want to get out of your room, ask for room service (but remember that again you will pay that) Romm service in good hotels is never cheap, just keep that in mind and ENJOY it.The hotel doesn't have a beach itself (they have an artificial one which is nice), but you do have oceanviews from the rooms.I would definately recommend this hotel. A+ for Mandarin Oriental in Miami.

<Content>Best Hotel in Miami Incredible. This is what MO is all about. If you don't need to be in South Beach proper, then definitely stay here.

<Author>OrrvilleRedRider
<Content>A Classy Hotel My wife, 8 year old son and I completed a very successful and enjoyable 7 night stay at the Mandarin Oriental, Miami on January 3, 2006. Our room was a Dynasty Suite on the 9th floor, comprised of a living room with sofa, 2 chairs, a coffee and end table, and a desk with a separate chair. The living room opened to a continuous balcony that extended past the bedroom (which also opened to the balcony) and wrapped around the corner of the hotel, so that we had views to both the west and north. There were built in cabinets on the wall of the living room for the TV and mini-bar. A powder room adjoined the living room. The living room appeared to be about the size of a normal double room at the hotel.Our bedroom 鈥?slightly smaller than the living room because of the curvature of the building, contained a wall of built in drawers and two closets, along with a king bed and two end tables. The bedroom adjoined the bathroom, which had a separate shower and tub and one sink. Although I would have preferred two sinks in the bathroom, the powder room off the living room proved helpful when both my wife and I needed a sink at the same time.All the appointments in both rooms were in keeping with a hotel of the highest quality. In contrast to some of the earlier reviews of the hotel I鈥檝e read on this site, all our furniture and floors were in excellent condition. Frette linens were in the bathroom (I didn鈥檛 check the sheets, but they were of the quality I鈥檇 expect of Frette).I鈥檓 a harsh critic of the tendency of some hotels to put 54 watt light bulbs in the fixtures so that the rooms are dim and unwelcoming. Although the Mandarin was not overly lit, the brightness and placement of the lighting both in the bedroom and the living room was such that I did not have a complaint. There were several locations in both rooms where I could easily read at night. Housekeeping was prompt and efficient 鈥?although turndown had not shown up one night when we returned from dinner at 9:45pm. The concierge staff was terrific. I relayed dinner reservation requests in advance, and the arrangements were handled perfectly. During our stay, 3 concierges were on duty most times during the 9am to 9 pm period.Caf茅 Sambal 鈥?the informal restaurant 鈥?was fine for breakfast, although the service was not quite up to Mandarin standards. The breakfast buffet was adequate (the baked goods and fruit selection were terrific, the hot foods a touch pedestrian). We ate dinner one night at Azul and had an excellent meal.Valet parking was decent. We retrieved our car 16 times during the stay, and on about 4 occasions had to wait 5 or more minutes even though I had called from the room before heading out. None of the waits was longer than 10 minutes, and on at least half the occasions the car was waiting for us when we made it the front door.The front desk operated efficiently. We were in our room within 5 minutes of arrival, and our luggage arrived almost simultaneously.My son and wife enjoyed the pool (it鈥檚 small, but perfectly adequate for an 8 year old) and beach (the staff didn鈥檛 blink an eyelid when my son decided to excavate rather than sunbathe).The public spaces were elegant and well appointed.Brickell Key, where the hotel is located, is mainly residential, and is in no way a hot spot for nightlife. That wasn鈥檛 a problem for us, since we weren鈥檛 interested in clubbing. Since we ate dinner each night at a different location (and never in Miami Beach), I found traffic to and from the hotel to be light.My only quibbles with the hotel would be (i) the lack of a separate easy chair in the bedroom, (ii) somewhat dirty furniture on the balcony and (iii) slightly disinterested service in Caf茅 Sambal. Not a bad quibble list for a week long stay, and the positives greatly outnumbered the negatives. I鈥檇 be pleased to have another stay at the Mandarin Oriental Miami.  
<Date>Jan 6, 2006

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Refined, Luxurious treat w/ World class friendly service Treated myself to a long weekend at the Mandarin for my birthday and it couldn't have been a better thing to do for myself. If you want refined elegance where service is with a welcoming smile, then this is it. Perfect for a meditative retreat - very restorative to the soul. The pool is not large, but it was never very crowded. It's an infinity pool so the views are nice, especially when you're in it. Water temp was always perfect. The constant refilling of ice water with lemon, gratis, was a most welcome touch for all the guests at the beach and pool. Pretty much did not need to leave the hotel as lazing by the pool and man-made beach w/ teak canopied beds was too perfect. Rooms were spacious and impeccably clean. Food at Cafe Azul was extemely good. High caliber fitness room (and of course their well-known spa which I did not try). There's also an easy jogging path around Key Brickell (about 1.3 miles) which the Mandarin gives a small map for. I've tried the Ritz Carlton in Miami as well with friends and I have to say I like them both equally but for different reasons. They are both high quality hotels well worth their 5 stars, but if you're looking for some privacy away from the crowds, then the Mandarin is a better bet. And yes, they brought me a lovely cake while I was away as well as received a lovely happy b-day message from their GM, Jorge Gonzales. Quite the nice surprise-- as I said their service seemed genuinely sincere and thoughtful. Would definitely stay again and plan to make this an annual trip. You really should try one of these wonderful hotels as it really does help to enhance the SOBE experience. Also try their web-site for some seasonal specials; you won't regret it.  
<Date>Aug 24, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Amazing hotel We stayed at the Mandarin Oriental in July for 5 nights and had a wonderful experience, for the most part. The room was beautiful with a view of the bay and had a large balcony. The bathroom was amazing; all marble with a stand-up shower, a bathtub for two and they provided the most wonderful bath products each day. We arrived quite late the first day, after midnight, and therefore ordered room service which was quite good and I didn't think badly priced ($15 for a huge chicken ceasar salad which we ended up sharing). We ate at Cafe Sambal every morning, the food and service was very good. Overall, the staff was wonderful, especially Carlos at the concierge desk, I cannot say enough good about him - he took care of all of our requests, some of which were a little extreme, with such ease and always with a smile. Everytime I picked up the phone for anything at all, I felt like someone was knocking on our door before I could hang up the receiver. Everywhere you go, the staff always stops to great you, from management all the way down the chain. The infinity pool was beautiful, get there early on the weekends before all of the chairs get taken though. The food / beverage service at the pool was a little spotty - we had to ask for a menu four times and wait 20 minutes for the waitress to finally come over. We ordered a cucumber - avocado roll and they forgot to roll the avocado in, when we brought that to their attention, they just put some chopped up avocado on top of the roll rather than roll a new one which was a little disappointing but in the scheme of things not a big deal at all.Our only complaint about our stay was when we had our final dinner at Azul, the only AAA 5 Diamond restaurant in all of Miami. We sat outside which I would not recommend unless it is a little cool because there is no air circulation at all. The food was wonderful, as a matter of fact it was the best meal we had down there and we consider ourseleves to have fairly sophisticated palates. The server who took care of us was, in the kindest word I can find, ATROCIOUS!!! We ate there on a Sunday evening and earlier in the day had brunch at the Biltmore where, anyone who has had the brunch there can tell you, you practically have to roll out of there you eat so much. Since we were not starving, we decided not to order an appetizer which our server clearly had a problem with, mind you this was right after we selected a $150 bottle of wine. Everytime we had a question about the menu, he had something obnoxious to say, for example when we were looking at the desert menu I asked what exactly the peach melba was, he responded with such attitude, It's peach! That was it for us and we made a complaint to the manager on duty and eventually followed up with the hotel General Manager the experience was so upsetting. Overall, we enjoyed the hotel very much but our experience at the restaurant always pops into my head when people ask about our mini vacation. We will definitely stay at the Mandarin Oriental again but we will NEVER eat at Azul again, there are so many wonderful resturants in Miami that will not treat you the way we were treated when you spend $300 on dinner so I suggest you spend your money elsewhere.  
<Date>Aug 23, 2005

The hotel didn't seem to be crowd at all even tho I was told it was booked solid. It could have been because of Hurricane Dennis. But the weather there was perfect. It didn't even rain.I would definitly stay again.

<Content>Top Hotel, wonderful experience My girlfriend and I stayed at the MO April 22-24. The minute you step into the lobby, this hotel will overwhelm you. The decor and even scents throughout are amazing. The service is the best I've ever experienced. All employees are constantly asking if everything is alright and if you need anything (almost to the point of annoyance, but very accomodating). Our original room had a small balcony compared to other rooms and we requested another room. A bellman was sent right away to meet us at our new room. The pool and pool area is a bit small for the size of the hotel, but no real complaints. The beach area is great. There is no access to the water, but there are nice mats set out and even raised beds with canopy for shade/privacy. I cannot comment about the food beyond breakfast and lunch at the pool as we ate out most nights, but it was very good (but also very pricey). The service was good, but slow at times.I would recommend this hotel to everyone. You definitely get what you pay for, which is a lot. There were two celebs staying at the hotel and even hanging around in the pool area. Was a bit awkward since everyone stared, but a new experience. I can't imagine staying at a better hotel.

<Author>NYCBeachBoy
<Content>No wonder it's number 1 From the moment I walked in the door til the moment I reluctantly checked out a week later, I enjoyed the Mandarin Oriental enormously. The decor everywhere is simply breathtaking. I had a beautiful king sized bed, a nice sitting area and a glorious bathroom with wonderful Moulton Brown toiletries. The quiet of the rooms is remarkable. The terrace with its skyline views was a wonderful place to chill out as was the lovely pool and the artificial beach. I also appreciated the absolute calm of the place and the crowd that stays there. Since this was a business trip, I needed the services of the Business Center and everything was handled with great efficiency and, like everything else at the Mandarin, the service is first rate.Even the maid service is remarkable. It seemed done before I even came back from breakfast...which is particularly nice when you are using your room for work part of the day. The turndown service was equally well timed--although I must confess to having provided one maid with a fully Monte when she came into the room after a single bell ring. The food is good but pricey. I found dining outdoors on the terrace perferable to the somewhat noisy Cafe Sambal. The Martini Bar off the lobby is fun. The pool Sushi bar is a great place for lunch. And then there's the spa. A truly wonderful place where I had a treatment that was simply unbelievably good and incredibly expensive. But I would have to say worth it. Finally for the guy who groused about the lack of nightlife, there's the Friday night party at the Beach--now one of the hottest tickets in Miami. The night we were there the crowd was gorgeous, swaying to latin music and just a lot of fun to watch. As a hotel guest, you have instant entree to what is a undoubtedly one of THE weekly events in Miami. Now one other thing....South Beach has had it. I have seldom seen such a really dreadful looking crowd anywhere--a lot of Europeans enjoying their inflated Euros and dressed so badly....it was very sad to see. We were initially supposed to be there but I am so glad we had the luxe and the splendour of the Mandarin to look forward to. I'd go back in a shot...even if I were paying for it myself.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Relaxing Stay I enjoyed a 2 night stay at the Mandarin on February 20th thru the 22nd. It felt luxurious walking into the lobby and seeing the great views of the bay and the skyline. My room was what I expected but I have to admit that the room size was not worth the price tag of $495 plus a night. Prices are high during this time due to peak season. I was welcomed with a greeting card and Joy of Life chocolates which were superb. The marble bathroom is fantastic and huge compared to most hotel bathrooms. I received the best service from the valet attendants, room service staff and maids. For example, I returned to my room while the maid was still there and I was going to go get some ice. The maid insisted on getting the ice for me and she did which was very nice. The valet attendants were very nice as well. The Front desk clerks were less attentive in their service. When I checked out, the front desk person didn't even ask how my stay was or if everything was met to my expectations. I also tried the Ayurvedic Holistic Body Treatment at the Spa in the Hotel and it was definately different than a regular swedish massage. I really enjoyed the spa lounge rooms with its sauna and steam room. The treatment room that I was in had it's own shower inside! I also ordered room service and the food was fine but nothing special. I would recommend getting the sorbet medley as a dessert since it was delicious with coconut, rasberry and mango. My stay was relaxing and very quiet. I never heard any noise from any of the rooms next to mine. The hotel is very close to all the freeways that lead to Miami Beach and you will get to Miami Beach in 15 minutes with no traffic. I noticed that traffic started between noon and up going to Miami Beach. Don't get scared away that you have to pay 20 or more for parking at Miami Beach. I parked at South Point Park for only $5.00 for all day and walked my way all along Ocean Drive and up South Beach. The real down side is that you have to pay $24 plus tax on valet parking at the hotel. The hotel is also located very close to Little Havana so you can grab lunch or dinner there too. I would stay at this hotel again since I did not experience any rude service or noisy atmosphere and the rooms were a delight.  
<Date>Feb 27, 2005

<Author>matthew.cronin
<Content>Sweet and Sour My wife and I stayed here for two nights in January, each separated by a week as we traveled abroad. The first night was fantastic, among the very best of our 2 week/4 country vacation. The room was huge and beautiful - filled with delicious incense as we entered for the first time. Room service was great and, I thought, very reasonably priced. The staff was very friendly and gracious (void of the South Beach attitude). We left the next morning very much looking forward to returning for another night a week later.Unfortunately when we returned we had a completely different experience. The staff seemed completely inundated with a conference that was being held there and we were obviously not the priority - we didn't even get assistance with our luggage. Our room was right next to the elevator despite the fact that I had specifically requested one away from the elevator (and it's in my 'profile' with MO). When I asked the manager if another room was available he said he could give me a suite for a good rate!!! They tried to up-sell me after giving me exactly what I had asked not to have - I felt like I had been scammed. An experience I would never have expected to have at a service oriented 5-star hotel.That experience burned me so bad I'm not sure I'd go back, despite having had a wonderful stay on the first night. My advice - ask if there will be a conference while you're there. If so, check out the new Four Seasons.

<Author>pal56
<Content>An Oasis My wife, 8 year old son and I had a wonderful stay at the Mandarin Oriental on January 4, 2005. Stunning architecture. We had a deluxe (five star) room with a great view of Biscayne Bay. The room was well appointed, stylish, clean with a comfortable bed, and large bathroom with a picture window into the bedroom. Bellman/valet service was excellent (we checked out at 4 am to catch an early flight and the car was waiting). The waiters at the resturant and at the pool provided prompt and pleasant service. The infinity pool and sand beach area are marvelous. The front desk service was friendly but below average for a hotel of this quality (computer was down at check-out and room needed a 30 minute inspection before we could complete somewhat early 1 pm check-in).The hotel is ideally located (on a small key) for access to the downtown Miami business district, but it's several miles from South Beach and Miami Beach. One negative is that during rush hour (4pm to 6:30 pm) traffic out of the downtown area is very heavy...it took us nearly 35 minutes just to get to I-95 at 5:45 pm on a Tuesday evening and almost 2 hours to get to Pro Players football stadium for the Orange Bowl.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Hotel Great, Staff service quite cold and unprepared First of all, I agree with most of the reviews on trip advisor that the hotel grounds and facilities are excellent. The staff however, could use a lesson or two on customer service and manners. In my opinion it's the service you receive that seperates the high end hotels from all the rest. The front desk clerks and concierge were of no help and were quite snobbish. We were in town for business, unfortunately during the time Hurricane Jeanne was due to hit north of Miami about 60 miles. Definitely not the time of year you want to be in Miami, and I realize we were lucky we didn't have a home in danger down there. I realize that it's not their choice to evacuate but when we were told at 10 am that we had to evacuate by noon and that they were not able to help in arranging an alternate hotel you realize you're not getting 5 star customer service. They gave us the names of hotels that they knew damn well didn't have any rooms available. Basically wasted our time on the phone when we should have been packing up to leave. I called down to the concierge and told him it would be well worth his time to help find us another hotel on the mainland and he basically blew me off with nothing I can do. No apologies or an attempt at being courteous. We later found out that other hotels on the water had reciprical arrangements with mainland hotels throughout the Miami area. You would think that a hotel that touts itself as Miami's finest, would be a bit more prepared for events such as this. You would expect this low level service from a cheaper hotel, not a highly touted 5 star establishment. Bottom line is, if you want to spend a lot of money and don't care about the poor service you receive this is the place.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nice Hotel but Poor Service I stayed at this property for three nights over Easter weekend. The property itself is nice other than the balcony which is not private, it has a screen which you can see through and see your neighbors you do. However the service leaves a lot to be desired. First at the beach area it took between 30 and 40 minutes to get a drink. This was every time you ordered a drink. When we received the drinks the plastic cup of champange had about 3 oz. of champagne, half full. Although it was a good quality of champange, Veuve Clicquot, I expect more than 3 oz. for $20. $20 is certainly an acceptable price if a proper glass is served with ample portion. Second, there are no umbrellas on the beach to block sun, however when I inquired prior to booking I was told they were available. Even the bellman when I arrived told me they had umbrellas on the beach. However the beach attendants will tell you they never had them. Third, the room service staff attempted to pick up the table from the balcony after breakfast and many glasses fell and broke. They never returned to clean up the broken glass. It took three calls and still no response. Finally a call to the manager on duty and an hour later it was cleaned up; that was at 8:00pm in the evening about ten hours after the incident occurred. The manager on duty, Ewon, did not display a positive guest service attitude or desire that the service be improved. I even phoned the general manager but he never even returned the call. On a postive note the breakfast was rather good. After all we decide to check out a day early and go over to the Ritz Carlton South Beach. It was amazing, what a difference great service makes. The staff at the Ritz where all over, smiling, asking if we needed anything, etc. You can really tell that they invest in their staff. If you go try to Club Floor its outstanding. It costs a little more than the Mandarian but its well worth the money.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>The Mighty Mandarin This hotel is absolutely wonderful in every respect (except for high winter time prices). It is well worth the usually high price tag. My last stay was about a year ago, but I still have terrific memories of the beautiful setting, the superbly appointed rooms, and the friendly staff. The room service breakfast is not to be missed -- each item, from the fruit salad to the wheat toast looks as if the chef has given it careful attention. The location could be inconvenient, if you're looking to spend all your time on South Beach. But if you have business downtown or on Brickell Key, it's perfect. Unless I'm on a budget (and heck, maybe even then), I would not miss an opportunity to stay at this hotel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>The best hotel in Miami ! My husband and I recently returned from Miami and stayed at the Mandarin Oriental. I love this hotel ! From the moment you walk in you feel zen. The colors were soothing and the view of Biscayne Bay was beautiful. We had a skyline water view room, nice size room and balcony. I fell in love with the bathroom, most hotels no longer have deep soaking tubs but the Mandarin did. While soaking in your tub you can also see the skyline/water view .. very nice. The service was excellent, if you needed something it was only a phone call away. The room did not have a cd player so I called and to my suprise they sent someone from engineering to put together a complete stereo system in my room. Another night we needed to use their business center and it was late. We called and they said it was closed but they would send someone to open it just for us. If you have a chance you must go down to their man made beach area, quite beautiful with all white canopy style beds with sheer curtains to make sunbathing that much more confortable. Order a tropical drink and relax. Overall we had a great time and that's the only hotel to stay at while in Miami.
